      <p><b>India</b> or the <b>Republic of India</b> (official name) is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. It has an area of 3,287,263 square kilometres (1,269,219&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It is at the center of <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>. India has more than 1.2 <a href="/wiki/Billion" class="mw-disambig" title="Billion">billion</a> (1,210,000,000) people, which is the second largest <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> in the <a href="/wiki/World" title="World">world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[15]</a></sup> It is the seventh largest country in the world by area and the largest country in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>. It is also the most populous <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw_-_India_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw_-_India-20">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_world's_largest_democratic_event:_India_begins_voting_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_world's_largest_democratic_event:_India_begins_voting-21">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-largestdem1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-largestdem1-22">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>India has seven neighbours: <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> in the north-west, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> in the north, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> in the north-east, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> in the east and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, an island, in the south. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Capital_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (city)">capital</a> of India is <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a>. India is a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a>, bound by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> in the south, the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a> on the west and <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> in the east. The <a href="/wiki/Coastline" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastline">coastline</a> of India is of about 7,517&nbsp;km (4,671&nbsp;mi) long.<sup id="cite_ref-sanilkumar_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sanilkumar-23">[19]</a></sup> India has the third largest <a href="/wiki/Indian_Armed_Forces" title="Indian Armed Forces">military force</a> in the world and is also a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapon</a> state.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>India's economy became the world's fastest growing in the <a href="/wiki/G20_developing_nations" title="G20 developing nations">G20 developing nations</a> in the last quarter of 2014, replacing the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-India_clocks_7.5%_growth_in_January-March_quarter,_becomes_world's_fastest_growing_economy_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India_clocks_7.5%_growth_in_January-March_quarter,_becomes_world's_fastest_growing_economy-25">[21]</a></sup> India's <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wealth" title="Wealth">wealth</a> are also rising.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[22]</a></sup> According to New World Wealth, India is the seventh richest country in the world with a total individual <a href="/wiki/Wealth" title="Wealth">wealth</a> of $5.6 trillion.<sup id="cite_ref-India_on_10_wealthiest_country_list,_takes_7th_spot_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India_on_10_wealthiest_country_list,_takes_7th_spot-27">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-India's_large_population_helps_push_it_to_7th_position_in_wealthiest_nations_list_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India's_large_population_helps_push_it_to_7th_position_in_wealthiest_nations_list-28">[24]</a></sup> However, it still has many <a href="/wiki/Social_issue" title="Social issue">social</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economic</a> issues like <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_India" title="Poverty in India">poverty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a>. India is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="World Trade Organisation">World Trade Organisation</a> (WTO), and has signed the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a>. </p>
      <p>India has the fourth largest number of spoken languages per country in the world, only behind <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[25]</a></sup> People of many different religions live there, including the five most popular world religions: <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>. The first three religions came from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> along with Jainism. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Symbols_of_India">National Symbols of India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: National Symbols of India">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: National Symbols of India">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_India.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Emblem_of_India.svg/220px-Emblem_of_India.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="374" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Emblem_of_India.svg/330px-Emblem_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Emblem_of_India.svg/440px-Emblem_of_India.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="331" data-file-height="562"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_India.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>National emblem of India
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The National emblem of India shows four <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a> standing back-to-back. The lions symbolise power, pride, confidence, and courage (bravery). Only the government can use this emblem, according to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_Emblem_of_India_(Prohibition_of_Improper_Use)_Act,_2005" class="extiw" title="en:State Emblem of India (Prohibition of Improper Use) Act, 2005">State Emblem of India (Prohibition of Improper Use) Act, 2005</a> </p>
      <p>The name India comes from the Greek word, <i>Indus</i>. This came from the word <i>sindhu</i>, which in time turned into Hind or <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">Hindi</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a>. The preferred native name or endonym is "Bharat" in <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and other Indian languages as contrasted with names from outsiders. Some of the national symbols are: </p>
      <p>National anthem- jana gana mana </p>
      <p>National song- vande mataram </p>
      <p>National animal- royal bengal tiger </p>
      <p>National bird- peacock </p>
      <p>National flower- lotus </p>
      <p>National tree- banyan </p>
      <p>National river- ganges(ganga) </p>
      <p>National fruit- mango </p>
      <p>National heritage animal- elephant </p>
      <p>National heritage bird- Indian Eagle </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg/220px-Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg/330px-Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg/440px-Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2040" data-file-height="1681"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Taj_Mahal" title="Taj Mahal">Taj Mahal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Agra" title="Agra">Agra</a> was built by Shah Jahan as a memorial to his wife <a href="/wiki/Mumtaz_Mahal" title="Mumtaz Mahal">Mumtaz Mahal</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> World Heritage Site. It is thought to be of "outstanding universal value".<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_TM_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO_TM-30">[26]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_India" title="History of India">History of India</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Two of the main classical languages of the world <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> language were born in India. Both of these languages are more than 3000 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[27]</a></sup> The country founded a <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a> called <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, which most Indians still follow. Later, a king named Chandragupt Maurya built an empire called the <a href="/wiki/Maurya_Empire" title="Maurya Empire">Maurya Empire</a> in 300 BC. It made most of <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> into one whole country.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[28]</a></sup> From 180 BC, many other countries invaded India. Even later (100 BC &nbsp;AD 1100), other Indian dynasties (empires) came, including the Chalukyas, Cholas, Pallavas, and Pandyas.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[29]</a></sup> Southern India at that time was famous for its science, art, and writing. The <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">Cholas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Thanjavur" title="Thanjavur">Thanjavur</a> were pioneers at war in the seas and invaded <a href="/wiki/Malaya" class="mw-disambig" title="Malaya">Malaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>. The influence of <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">Cholas</a> are still well noticeable in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">SE Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">dynasties</a> ruled India around the year 1000. Some of these were the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">Vijayanagara</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Maratha_dynasty" title="Maratha dynasty">Maratha</a> empires. In the 1600s, European countries invaded India, and the British controlled most of India by 1856.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early 1900s, <a href="/wiki/Million" title="Million">millions</a> of people peacefully started to <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/protest" class="extiw" title="wikt:protest">protest</a> against British control. One of the people who led the freedom movement was <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a>, who only used peaceful tactics, including a way called "<a href="/wiki/Ahimsa" title="Ahimsa">ahimsa</a>", which means "non-violence".<sup id="cite_ref-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_3_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_3-36">[32]</a></sup> On 15 August 1947, India peacefully became free and independent from the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. India's <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a> was founded on 26 January 1950. Every year, on this day, Indians celebrate Republic Day. The first official leader (<a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a>) of India was <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a>. </p>
      <p>After 1947, India had a socialist planned economy. It is one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. It has fought many <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">wars</a> since independence from <a href="/wiki/Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Britain">Britain</a>, including the wars in 1947-48, 1965, 1971, and 1999 with <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and in 1962 with <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">China</a>. It also fought a war to capture <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a>-built <a href="/wiki/Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbour">port</a> and a city which was not a part of India until 1961. The Portuguese refused to give it to the country, and so India had to use force and the Portuguese were defeated. India has also done nuclear tests in 1974 and 1998, and it is one of the few countries that has <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear bomb">nuclear bombs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-India_is_a_Nuclear_State_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India_is_a_Nuclear_State-37">[33]</a></sup> Since 1991, India has been one of the fastest-growing economies in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Government">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Government">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:New_Delhi_government_block_03-2016_img3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/New_Delhi_government_block_03-2016_img3.jpg/220px-New_Delhi_government_block_03-2016_img3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/New_Delhi_government_block_03-2016_img3.jpg/330px-New_Delhi_government_block_03-2016_img3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/New_Delhi_government_block_03-2016_img3.jpg/440px-New_Delhi_government_block_03-2016_img3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5136" data-file-height="2568"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:New_Delhi_government_block_03-2016_img3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Parliament of India.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>India is the largest <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-largestdem1_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-largestdem1-22">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>India's government is divided into three parts: the Legislative (the one that makes the laws, the Parliament), the Executive (the government), and the Judiciary (the one that makes sure that the laws are obeyed, the supreme court). </p>
      <p>The legislative branch is made up of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">Parliament</a> of India, which is in <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a>, the capital of India. The Parliament of India is divided into two houses: the upper house, Rajya Sabha (Council of States); and the lower house, Lok Sabha (House of People). The Rajya Sabha has 250 members,<sup id="cite_ref-Parliament_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parliament-39">[35]</a></sup> and the Lok Sabha has 552 members.<sup id="cite_ref-Parliament_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parliament-39">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The executive branch is made up of the <a href="/wiki/President" title="President">President</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vice_President" class="mw-redirect" title="Vice President">Vice President</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a>, and the Council of Ministers. The President of India is elected for a period of five years. The President can choose the Prime Minister, who has most of the power. The Council of Ministers, such as the Minister of Defence, help the Prime Minister. Narendra Modi became the Prime Minister of India on May 16, 2014. He is the 19th Prime Minister of India. The president has less power than the prime minister. </p>
      <p>The judicial branch is made up of the <a href="/wiki/Court" title="Court">courts</a> of India, including the Supreme Court. The Chief Justice of India is the head of the Supreme Court. Supreme Court members have the power to stop a law being passed by Parliament if they think that the law is illegal and contradicts (opposes) the <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">Constitution</a> of India.<sup id="cite_ref-Manorama_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manorama-40">[36]</a></sup> In India, there are also 24 High Courts. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography and climate">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: Geography and climate">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Indiarivers.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Indiarivers.png/220px-Indiarivers.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Indiarivers.png/330px-Indiarivers.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/97/Indiarivers.png 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="402"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Indiarivers.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rivers of India
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>India is the seventh biggest country in the world. It is the main part of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_the_Republic_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Borders of the Republic of India">countries next to India</a> are <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>. It is also near <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">island</a> country. </p>
      <p>India is a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a>, which means that it is surrounded on three sides by water. One of the seven wonders of the world is in Agra: the Taj Mahal. In the west is the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a>, in the south is the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, and in the east is the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>. The northern part of India has many mountains. The most famous mountain range in India is the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>, which have some of the tallest <a href="/wiki/Mountain" title="Mountain">mountains</a> in the world. There are many rivers in India. The main rivers are the <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">Ganges</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brahmaputra_River" title="Brahmaputra River">Brahmaputra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Yamuna" title="Yamuna">Yamuna</a>, the Godavari, the Kaveri, the Narmada, and the Krishna. </p>
      <p>India has different climates.<sup id="cite_ref-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_4_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_4-41">[37]</a></sup> In the South, the climate is mainly tropical, which means it can get very hot in summer and cool in winter.<sup id="cite_ref-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_4_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_4-41">[37]</a></sup> The northern part, though, has a cooler climate, called sub-tropical, and even alpine in mountainous regions.<sup id="cite_ref-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_4_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_4-41">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>, in the alpine climate region, can get extremely cold. There is very heavy <a href="/wiki/Rainfall" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainfall">rainfall</a> along the west coast and in the Eastern Himalayan foothills. The west, though, is drier. Because of some of the <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">deserts</a> of India, all of India gets rain for four months of the year. That time is called the monsoon. That is because the deserts attract water-filled winds from the Indian Ocean, which give rain when they come into India. When the monsoon rains come late or not so heavily, <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">droughts</a> (when the land dries out because there is less rain) are possible. Monsoons normally come around July - August. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Defence">Defence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Defence">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Defence">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indian_Armed_Forces" title="Indian Armed Forces">Indian Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <b>Indian Armed Forces</b> is the military of India. It is made up of an <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Navy" title="Indian Navy">Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">Air Force</a>. There are other parts like Paramilitary and Strategic Nuclear Command. </p>
      <p>The President of India is the Commander-in-Chief. However, it is managed by the Ministry of Defence. In 2010, the Indian Armed Forces had 1.32 million active personnel. This makes it one of the largest militaries in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Indian Army is becoming more modern by buying and making new weapons. It is also building defenses against missiles of other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[39]</a></sup> In 2011, India imported more weapons than any other nation in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From its independence in 1947, India fought four wars with Pakistan and a war with China. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_states">Indian states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Indian states">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: Indian states">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>For <a href="/wiki/Administration" class="mw-disambig" title="Administration">administration</a> purposes, India has been divided into smaller pieces. Most of these pieces are called <a href="/wiki/State" title="State">states</a>, some are called <a href="/wiki/Union_territory" title="Union territory">union territories</a>. States and union territories are different in the way they are represented. Most union territories are ruled by administrators sent by the central government. All the states, and the territories of Delhi, and Puducherry <a href="/wiki/Election" title="Election">elect</a> their local government themselves. In total, there are twenty-eight states, and nine union territories.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_PROFILE_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_PROFILE-45">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <a href="/wiki/File:IndiaStatesByRTOcodes.png" class="image" title="These are the states and territories of India, including 29 states and 7 union territories."><img alt="These are the states and territories of India, including 29 states and 7 union territories." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/IndiaStatesByRTOcodes.png/300px-IndiaStatesByRTOcodes.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="350" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/IndiaStatesByRTOcodes.png/450px-IndiaStatesByRTOcodes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/IndiaStatesByRTOcodes.png/600px-IndiaStatesByRTOcodes.png 2x" data-file-width="1487" data-file-height="1735"></a>
      </div>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trouble_with_the_borders">Trouble with the borders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Trouble with the borders">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Trouble with the borders">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>There are <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/dispute" class="extiw" title="wikt:dispute">disputes</a> about certain parts of the Indian borders. Countries do not agree on where the borders are.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> do not recognise the disputed territory of <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir" class="mw-redirect" title="Jammu and Kashmir">Jammu and Kashmir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ipbdMOI_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipbdMOI-47">[43]</a></sup> The Indian government claims it as an Indian state.<sup id="cite_ref-ipbdMOI_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipbdMOI-47">[43]</a></sup> Similarly, the Republic of India does not recognise the Pakistani and Chinese parts of Kashmir.<sup id="cite_ref-ipbdMOI_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipbdMOI-47">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1914, <a href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> agreed on the <a href="/wiki/McMahon_Line" title="McMahon Line">McMahon Line</a>, as part of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Simla_Accord_(1914)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Simla Accord (1914) (not yet started)">Simla Accord</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-simlaCFR_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-simlaCFR-48">[44]</a></sup> In July 1914, China withdrew from the agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-simlaCFR_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-simlaCFR-48">[44]</a></sup> Indians and Tibetans see this line as the official border. China does not agree, and both mainland China and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> do not recognize that Arunachal Pradesh belongs to India. According to them, it is a part of <a href="/wiki/South_Tibet" title="South Tibet">South Tibet</a>, which belongs to China.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IPCS_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCS-50">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Economy">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Economy">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_India" title="Economy of India">Economy of India</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy of the country is among the world's fastest growing. It is the 7th largest in the world with a nominal <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dollar" title="Dollar">$</a>2,250 billion (<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>), and in terms of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a>, the economy is 3rd largest (worth $8.720 trillion USD).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[47]</a></sup> The growth rate is 8.25% for fiscal 2010. However, that is still $3678 (considering PPP) per person per year. India's economy is based mainly on: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Service_sector" title="Service sector">Service sector</a>: 43%</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Industries">Industries</a>: 41%</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">Information technology</a>: 7%</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Farming" title="Farming">Farming</a>: 7%</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Outsourcing" title="Outsourcing">Outsourcing</a>: 2%.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>India's economy is diverse. Major industries include <a href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">automobiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cement" title="Cement">cement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemical" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemical">chemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machinery" class="mw-redirect" title="Machinery">machinery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharmaceuticals">pharmaceuticals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation">transportation</a> equipment, and <a href="/wiki/Textiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Textiles">textiles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-52">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, despite economic growth, India continues to suffer from <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_India" title="Poverty in India">poverty</a>. 27.5% of the population was living in poverty in 2004–2005.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[49]</a></sup> In addition, 80.4% of the population live on less than USD $2 a day,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[50]</a></sup> which was lowered to 68% by 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: People">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: People">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:India_population_density_map_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/India_population_density_map_en.svg/220px-India_population_density_map_en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/India_population_density_map_en.svg/330px-India_population_density_map_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/India_population_density_map_en.svg/440px-India_population_density_map_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1639" data-file-height="1852"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:India_population_density_map_en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>This is a map of the <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> of India.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are 1.21 billion people living in India.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[52]</a></sup> India is the second largest country by the number of people living in it, with China being the first. Experts think that by the year 2030, India will be the first.<sup id="cite_ref-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_2_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONCISE_ENCYCLOPEDIA_2-57">[53]</a></sup> About 65% of Indians live in <a href="/wiki/Rural_area" title="Rural area">rural areas</a>, or land set aside for farming.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-58">[54]</a></sup> The largest <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">cities</a> in India are <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_India" title="Hyderabad, India">Hyderabad</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ahmedabad" title="Ahmedabad">Ahmedabad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_PROFILE_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_PROFILE-45">[41]</a></sup> India has 23 official languages.<sup id="cite_ref-languagesofInd_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-languagesofInd-59">[55]</a></sup> Altogether, 1,625 languages are spoken in India.<sup id="cite_ref-Manorama_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manorama-40">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Languages">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Languages">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>There are many different languages and <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultures</a> in India. The only geographical place with more different languages and cultures is the <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African continent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_PROFILE_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_PROFILE-45">[41]</a></sup> There are two main language families in India, the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_languages" title="Dravidian languages">Dravidian languages</a>. About 69% of Indians speak an Indo-Arayan language, about 26% speak a Dravidian language. Other languages spoken in India come from the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Austro-Asiatic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Austro-Asiatic languages (not yet started)">Austro-Asiatic</a> group. Around 5% of the people speak a <a href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman_languages" title="Tibeto-Burman languages">Tibeto-Burman</a> language. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> is the official language in India with the largest number of speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[56]</a></sup> It is the official language of the union.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup> Native speakers of Hindi represent about 41% of the Indian population (2001 Indian census). English is also used, mostly for business and in the administration. It has the status of a 'subsidiary official language'.<sup id="cite_ref-English-subsidiary_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-English-subsidiary-62">[58]</a></sup> The constitution also recognises 21 other languages. Either many people speak those languages, or they have been recognised to be very important for Indian culture. The number of <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/dialect" class="extiw" title="wikt:dialect">dialects</a> in India is as high as 1,652.<sup id="cite_ref-Manorama_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manorama-40">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the south of India, many people speak <a href="/wiki/Kannada" title="Kannada">Kannada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu" title="Telugu">Telugu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a>. In the north, many people speak <a href="/wiki/Chhattisgarh" title="Chhattisgarh">Chhattisgarhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Odia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Odia (not yet started)">Odia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihari</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pandit1977_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pandit1977-63">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica1993_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica1993-64">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>India has 23 official languages. Its constitution lists the name of the country in each of the languages.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> (listed in boldface) are the "official languages of the union" (Union meaning the Federal Government in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>);<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>,<a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu" title="Telugu">Telugu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kannada" title="Kannada">Kannada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Odia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Odia (not yet started)">Odia</a> are officially the "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Classical_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Classical language (not yet started)">classical languages of India</a>." </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <p><a href="/wiki/Cave_painting" title="Cave painting">Cave paintings</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> are found across India. They show <a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">dances</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ritual" title="Ritual">rituals</a> and suggest there was a <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">prehistoric</a> religion. During the Epic and <a href="/wiki/Purana" title="Purana">Puranic</a> periods, the earliest versions of the epic poems <i><a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">Mahabharata</a></i> were written from about 500–100 BCE,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[64]</a></sup> although these were <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/oral" class="extiw" title="wikt:oral">orally</a> <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/transmission" class="extiw" title="wikt:transmission">transmitted</a> for centuries before this period.<sup id="cite_ref-Rine28_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rine28-69">[65]</a></sup> Other <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a> Stone Age sites apart from <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> are in modern India, such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bhimbetka_rock_shelters&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bhimbetka rock shelters (not yet started)">Bhimbetka rock shelters</a> in central <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a> and the Kupgal petroglyphs of eastern Karnataka, contain rock art showing religious rites and evidence of possible <a href="/wiki/Ritual" title="Ritual">ritualised</a> music.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Golden_Temple_India.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Golden_Temple_India.jpg/175px-Golden_Temple_India.jpg" decoding="async" width="175" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Golden_Temple_India.jpg/263px-Golden_Temple_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Golden_Temple_India.jpg/350px-Golden_Temple_India.jpg 2x" data-file-width="963" data-file-height="723"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Golden_Temple_India.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Harmandir Sahib or The Golden Temple of the <a href="/wiki/Sikh" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikh">Sikhs</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Several modern religions are linked to India,<sup id="cite_ref-EB_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-71">[67]</a></sup> namely modern <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>. All of these religions have different <i>schools</i> (ways of thinking) and <a href="/wiki/Tradition" class="mw-redirect" title="Tradition">traditions</a> that are related. As a group they are called the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_religions" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern religions">Eastern religions</a>. The Indian religions are similar to one another in many ways: The basic beliefs, the way <a href="/wiki/Worship" title="Worship">worship</a> is done and several religious practices are very similar. These similarities mainly come from the fact that these religions have a common history and common origins. They also influenced each other. </p>
      <p>The religion of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is the main faith followed by 79.80% of people in the Republic of India; <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> – 14.23%; <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> – 2.30%; Sikhism – 1.72%; <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> – 0.70% and <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> – 0.37%.<sup id="cite_ref-CensusRel_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CensusRel-72">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It's the first time ever since independence that Hindu population percentage fell below 80%. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Technology">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Change section: Technology">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>India sent a spacecraft to <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> for the first time in 2014. That made it the third country and only Asian country to do so, successfully. India is the only country to be successful in its very first attempt to orbit Mars. It was called the Mars Orbiter Mission. </p>
      <p>ISRO launched 104 satellites in a single mission to create world record. India became the first nation in the world to have launched over a hundred satellites in one mission. That was more than the 2014 Russian record of 37 satellites in a single launch. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pop_culture">Pop culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Pop culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Change section: Pop culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>India has the largest movie industry in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">source?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[69]</a></sup> Based in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Bombay" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombay">Bombay</a>), the industry is also known as <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>. It makes 1,000 movies a year, about twice as many as Hollywood.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup> It produces movies almost everyday. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=14" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Sports">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Change section: Sports">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:IPL_T20_Chennai_vs_Kolkata.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Cricketers in a game in front of nearly-full stands." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/IPL_T20_Chennai_vs_Kolkata.JPG/220px-IPL_T20_Chennai_vs_Kolkata.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/IPL_T20_Chennai_vs_Kolkata.JPG/330px-IPL_T20_Chennai_vs_Kolkata.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/IPL_T20_Chennai_vs_Kolkata.JPG/440px-IPL_T20_Chennai_vs_Kolkata.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:IPL_T20_Chennai_vs_Kolkata.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A 2008 Indian Premier League Twenty20 cricket match being played between the Chennai Super Kings and Kolkata Knight Riders
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_India" title="Sports in India">Sports in India</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Indians have excelled in Hockey. They have also won eight gold, one silver and two bronze medals at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_games" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic games">Olympic games</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> is the most popular sport in India. The Indian cricket team won the 1983 and <a href="/wiki/2011_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2011 Cricket World Cup">2011 Cricket World Cup</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_ICC_World_Twenty20&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2007 ICC World Twenty20 (not yet started)">2007 ICC World Twenty20</a>. They <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/share" class="extiw" title="wikt:share">shared</a> the 2002 ICC Champions Trophy with <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> and won the 2013 ICC Champions Trophy.Cricket in India is controlled by the Board of Control for Cricket in India or BCCI. Domestic tournaments are the Ranji Trophy, the Duleep Trophy, the Deodhar Trophy, the Irani Trophy and the Challenger Series. There is also the Indian cricket league and Indian premier league Twenty20 competitions. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">Tennis</a> has become popular due to the victories of the India Davis Cup team. <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is also a popular sport in northeast India, West Bengal, Goa and Kerala.<sup id="cite_ref-Soccer_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soccer-75">[71]</a></sup> The Indian national football team has won the South Asian Football Federation Cup many times. <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">Chess</a>, which comes from India, is also becoming popular. This is with the increase in the number of Indian Grandmasters.<sup id="cite_ref-Anand_crowned_World_champion_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anand_crowned_World_champion-76">[72]</a></sup> Traditional sports include kabaddi, kho kho, and gilli-danda, which are played throughout India. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=15" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Notes">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Change section: Notes">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="column-width: 30em; -moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <ol class="references"> 
        <li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-5">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">"[...] <i>Jana Gana Mana</i> is the National Anthem of India, subject to such alterations in the words as the Government may authorise as occasion arises; and the song <i>Vande Mataram</i>, which has played a historic part in the struggle for Indian freedom, shall be honoured equally with <i>Jana Gana Mana</i> and shall have equal status with it."(<a href="#CITEREFConstituent_Assembly_of_India1950">Constituent Assembly of India 1950</a>).</span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-8">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">According to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Part_XVII_of_the_Constitution_of_India&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Part XVII of the Constitution of India (not yet started)">Part XVII of the Constitution of India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Standard_Hindi" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Hindi">Hindi</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Devanagari" title="Devanagari">Devanagari</a> script is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of the Union, along with <a href="/wiki/Indian_English" title="Indian English">English</a> as an additional official language.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Home_Affairs_1960_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Home_Affairs_1960-6">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Informatics_Centre2005_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Informatics_Centre2005-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-india.gov.in2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-india.gov.in2-7">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India" title="States and union territories of India">States and union territories</a> can have a different official language of their own other than Hindi or English.</span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-11">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">"The country's exact size is subject to debate because some borders are disputed. The Indian government lists the total area as 3,287,260&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,269,220&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and the total land area as 3,060,500&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,181,700&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi); the United Nations lists the total area as 3,287,263&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,269,219&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and total land area as 2,973,190&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,147,960&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)."(<a href="#CITEREFLibrary_of_Congress2004">Library of Congress 2004</a>).</span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-18">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">See <a href="/w/index.php?title=Date_and_time_notation_in_India&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Date and time notation in India (not yet started)">Date and time notation in India</a>.</span> </li>
